<div id="review_114944685" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114944685" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114944685?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444710779" href="/book/show/7895644-my-name-is-memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=alternating-m-f-pov">alternating-m-f-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=i-thought-i-would-love-this-but">i-thought-i-would-love-this-but</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114944685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8970235595982341980">At first I wasn't sure if I would read it all - the first chapter, while definitely compelling, is pretty intense with the depth of romance and the soul mate connection thing and I wasn't sure if it was a too hard-core love story for my taste...<br/><br/>However, it swiftly moves along in chapters that not only alternate in POV, but also in time periods including ancient settings and exotic and varied locations around the world. While a lot of these chapters recounted the love and history between Daniel a</span>
  <span id="freeText8970235595982341980" style="display:none">At first I wasn't sure if I would read it all - the first chapter, while definitely compelling, is pretty intense with the depth of romance and the soul mate connection thing and I wasn't sure if it was a too hard-core love story for my taste...<br /><br />However, it swiftly moves along in chapters that not only alternate in POV, but also in time periods including ancient settings and exotic and varied locations around the world. While a lot of these chapters recounted the love and history between Daniel and Sophie (Lucy) they were not so focused on the love, but on the tragedy.<br /><br />Reading Daniel's chapters had the feel of reading a fable and stories of old, lyrical and sometimes powerful. The writing had a lovely lilting feel to it.<br /><br />What I liked:<br /><br />The settings. Brashares really did an outstanding job of taking the story around the world and each time period felt authentic.<br /><br />I loved the little stories of past lives, people long gone, often having lived a haunting tale. There were some moving anecdotes and scenes hidden in there.<br /><br />The whole way she created her reincarnation-lore was pretty awesome and intriguing and it made a cool premise. Yeah, I think she pulled it off.<br />It's impressive, all she fit in, from war to ancient times to college and the early 1900's Each time period felt authentic and fresh.<br /><br /><br />What I would have liked:<br /><br />Would it have been too much to add in a little humour of light-heartedness for some levity? After a while, I was all, 'this is so damn depressing'. Tragedy after haunted moment after fated circumstance and just-missed-it timing. <br /><br />It's not a funny book. Okay, that's stating the obvious, but I seriously did not smile or laugh once. Okay, I may have smirked in a passionate moment, haha. What can I say, occasional melodrama amuses me. I always like to have a little smile every now and then while reading, just saying.<br /><br />Towards the end, I felt Daniel's lives were all a blur of depression, he felt soul-weary and I can't think of things he enjoyed in life apart from thinking about Sophie and pining for her. He felt like he was narrating the tragedy's of his life. Was their love really that strong that everything pales in comparison? Although, he did occasionally impress me with glimpses of talent and every now and then he surprised me with something resembling a personality. Haha.<br /><br />Why do hard-core romance books sometimes make me feel cynical? I should be ashamed of myself.<br /><br /><br />Recommended: If you love romance and haunting stories of ancient lives, this is definitely for you. Seriously, I can think of people who would love this. It's got the potential to have girls swooning over the tortured soul who loves his girl with his whole being to die for her (I am not being cynical here, really). Also, it's got a fabulous premise and is well written :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8970235595982341980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_109099862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109099862" />
    <a title="Dwayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3273496-dwayne"><img alt="Dwayne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266450721p2/3273496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109099862?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dwayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dwayne" href="/user/show/3273496-dwayne">Dwayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109099862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5024059564264418310">Reviewed @ <a href='http://withoutabookshelf.blogspot.com/2010/06/book-review-my-name-is-memory-ann.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girls Without a Bookshelf.</a><br/><br/>I read quite a lot of romance, and I do like most of them, but occasionally I find one that can easily outclass the rest. My Name is Memory is in huge contention for the most romantic book I have ever laid hands on.<br/><br/>The story of Daniel is one that is both fascinating and unnerving. I found the concept of reincarnation common enough, but to carry the memory of it all - both a gift and a curse to our hero - is a fresh albeit as intriguing twist to the idea. The </span>
  <span id="freeText5024059564264418310" style="display:none">Reviewed @ <a href="http://withoutabookshelf.blogspot.com/2010/06/book-review-my-name-is-memory-ann.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Girls Without a Bookshelf.</a><br /><br />I read quite a lot of romance, and I do like most of them, but occasionally I find one that can easily outclass the rest. My Name is Memory is in huge contention for the most romantic book I have ever laid hands on.<br /><br />The story of Daniel is one that is both fascinating and unnerving. I found the concept of reincarnation common enough, but to carry the memory of it all - both a gift and a curse to our hero - is a fresh albeit as intriguing twist to the idea. The complexity of Daniel's memory is engaging and intensely captivating, and as more of his history is introduced I was felt I was being enlightened to a philosophical, cosmic law. I was curious as to how the plot would present the concept of reincarnation and the accompanying memory - I did have a lot of questions but these has been more or less seen to in the course of the plot.<br /><br />The novel is in alternate chapters of past and present. Through Daniel's account, readers glimpse his - and Lucy's/Sophia's - history. Images of the past were new and exciting to me. I cannot comment on the accuracy of the depictions but I am pretty satisfied and as Daniel is more thoughts than acts it is really his reflections which captivated me.I looked forward to each chapter of Daniel's narration and history while reading the present events and looked forward to the present while I was immersed in each of Daniel's chapters. Once I started reading, I almost haven't stopped.<br /><br />Daniel is certainly the mostnotable character. It is easy to feel - yes, feel - him in every page. His character is thoughful, reflective, almost self-less. He carries in his narration the words of a man who has lived a hundred lives, and this I felt is what drew me most to his character. It was as if a tangible Daniel has written those accounts himself; the emotions and anguish were so raw, his love for Lucy pervades his every word. It is worth noting, I think, that whilst Daniel is unquestionably in love with Lucy, he lives each of his life as his own person. Whilst Lucy is also a developed character, I find the balance tilted more towards Daniel. In a way, I think the latter surpasses many of the characters I have come to admire; there is respectability and a sort of magnetic admirability in Daniel that I rarely, if ever, find in others.<br /><br />Now, if that was not enough, the twist in the plot had me gasping, squealing and racing to find out what happens next. It was incredible. The suspense was almost heartbreaking; I wasn't quite sure how everything would fall in place!<br /><br />And while the ending(or lack thereof) was impossibly vague, it was not frustrating at all. I was still basking in the intensity of Daniel and Lucy's love to be frustrated about anything at all. I absolutely adore this novel. I could not get enough, and whilst I'm not sure if there will be a sequel, I damn well hope so.<br /><br />I still re-read my favourite parts and am yet to determine how to untangle myself from this novel. It's impossible not to fall in love with it!<br /><br />My Name is Memory is beautiful,beautiful novel. Written exceedingly well, with magnetic characters and with a romance that took my breath - and my heart - away, it is easily the most romantic novel I have read as of late.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5024059564264418310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_100445523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100445523" />
    <a title="Athira (Reading on a Rainy Day)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day"><img alt="Athira (Reading on a Rainy Day)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303004785p2/2543022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100445523?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Athira (Reading on a Rainy Day)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Athira (Reading on a Rainy Day)" href="/user/show/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day">Athira (Reading on a Rainy Day)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=source-own">source-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=f-general">f-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=aud-ya">aud-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=source-review">source-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=list-series">list-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=format-print">format-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543022-athira-reading-on-a-rainy-day?shelf=f-romance">f-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100445523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10067647957711441639">Daniel has been looking for the same girl for centuries. He first saw her in 541 AD. Since then, he has come across her in several of their future lives. He remembers her; she doesn't. In their current lives, Daniel and the girl, Lucy, attend the same high school. She is smitten by him but they do not get a chance to talk until prom night, when an incident at school puts the two of them in the same room. That night when they kiss, Lucy is frightened both by the images that come to her mind and b</span>
  <span id="freeText10067647957711441639" style="display:none">Daniel has been looking for the same girl for centuries. He first saw her in 541 AD. Since then, he has come across her in several of their future lives. He remembers her; she doesn't. In their current lives, Daniel and the girl, Lucy, attend the same high school. She is smitten by him but they do not get a chance to talk until prom night, when an incident at school puts the two of them in the same room. That night when they kiss, Lucy is frightened both by the images that come to her mind and by Daniel's insistence in calling her Sophia.<br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised that I enjoyed this book quite a lot. It is not exactly my usual genre, and there were some aspects that did turn me off. But in the end, I am truly glad to have read this book.<br /><br />At the outset, this book accepts that when people die, their souls come back as a different person. Not exactly something I would believe in, so you can see why it is not my usual genre. I find it easy reading science, or steampunk, or dystopian fiction, but when it comes to souls and afterlife and rebirth, I usually go uh-uh. Although I was expecting to be bothered by that, I found it rather easy to accept the "principles" of life in this book. Maybe because there is no talk of religion or because there is no hand of God in any of these happenings. Far from it, it happens to be the accepted way of life, and very few of them retain memories from their old lives. Kind of like recycling - instead of paper, souls go through that process here.<br /><br />Being as it is composed of fantastic ingredients, there will always be questions about how anything happens in this book - be it soul "recycling", or how Daniel's memory is intact but not many of the others'. I wasn't entirely satisfied with some of these answers, but Daniel himself admits to being unaware or unsure of them. Another thing that bothered me quite a lot, was the ease with which Daniel gave up his lives - most of the times for Sophia. Maybe if I knew that I will be born again, I may be just as lax, but it makes me cringe, when he does it just because he "loves" a woman with whom he hasn't spent much time together. The "love" Daniel feels for Sophia is fascinating, and when one has lived for centuries the way Daniel has, priorities probably take shape, and Daniel's must have been Sophia. But I would have appreciated to see a little more respect towards the life he had at the moment. This is a debatable point, and I have kept vacillating against and in defense of Daniel, but it makes me wonder, if we had all of eternity to live, would we be just as indifferent to life? (Somehow a part of me tells 'yes'.)<br /><br />Daniel and Sophia's story is actually quite pleasing to read about. Although none of Sophia's "lives" initially falls for Daniel's insistence that he has known her for centuries, I'm sure my reaction would be far more outrageous than Sophia's. A story like this wouldn't be complete without a villain, and we have Daniel's brother (in one of his lives) take that role, due to a shared history in which Daniel's brother came off as the loser.<br /><br /><i>My Name is Memory</i> is an adult book, but I was very disappointed with the writing. I found it too simplistic, sometimes repetitive, and almost always the two characters behaved like fifteen-year olds. The dialogue at many points was too cheesy. This is disappointing because this book has a good idea which Ann Brashares has executed well. If the writing was better, I would have enjoyed it more.<br /><br />I understand that this is the first book in a trilogy, and sure, the battle is far from over. But much of this book is slow, since there is a lot of history doled out to show the emotional or spiritual connection between Daniel and Sophia. I expected an ambiguous ending, but I can't say I am exactly eager to grab the next book in the trilogy. The cliffhanger wasn't so much one. So while I may choose to read the next book some time, I won't be exactly impatient for it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10067647957711441639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241799190?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/5237607-sophia">Sophia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340953518" href="/book/show/8480676-my-name-is-memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237607-sophia?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237607-sophia?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237607-sophia?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237607-sophia?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237607-sophia?shelf=all-time-favorite">all-time-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237607-sophia?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241799190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3430419372757597892">What does it feel knowing the things that happened in your previous life <i>(being reincarnated with Memory)</i>? What will you do to continue living like an ordinary human? Would you consider that having the Memory is a way of redoing things that you regret before? Or would you regret on living with your Memory again? Would you do the same things you did before just to be sure that you’re still the same person in your first life? Would you still search for someone who became your anchor in your past l</span>
  <span id="freeText3430419372757597892" style="display:none">What does it feel knowing the things that happened in your previous life <i>(being reincarnated with Memory)</i>? What will you do to continue living like an ordinary human? Would you consider that having the Memory is a way of redoing things that you regret before? Or would you regret on living with your Memory again? Would you do the same things you did before just to be sure that you’re still the same person in your first life? Would you still search for someone who became your anchor in your past lives?<br /><br />Those are some of the questions that I’d asked before reading this book. My Name Is Memory is a great way of picturing the mystery of reincarnation. It is a must read for believers <i>(like me)</i> and non-believers who question the necessity of erasing the soul’s memories of its past lives. The story combined many facets of what is possible in life and love in all time. This book reminds me of <i>Audrey Niffeneger’s Time Traveler’s Wife.</i> <br /><br />It’s a fresh read to me, perhaps Ann Brashares chose the right words at the right time. I don’t usually read romantic books and I didn't regret that I bought and read this paperback. <br /><br />I felt a pang towards the end of the book, because I’m definitely sure that there would be a cliff hanger. And there is. The ending is so ambiguous that I hope there <s>should</s> must be a sequel.<br /><br />To sum it all, its a great novel and its on my favorite books this 2011.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3430419372757597892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11166064693863994551"> "I read Fallen by Lauren Kate, then I read this one later that week. The similarities are striking. First, there is the unrequited love thing going where Daniel (same name and everything) loves Lucy (in fallen, it was Luce) for thousands of years. He remembers, she doesn't. That in itself is interesting. Luckily, the similarities end there, as I really did not like Fallen, if I could have given it negative stars I would have. However, I would give My Name is Memory 4. There were a few notable d</span>
  <span id="freeText11166064693863994551" style="display:none"> "I read Fallen by Lauren Kate, then I read this one later that week. The similarities are striking. First, there is the unrequited love thing going where Daniel (same name and everything) loves Lucy (in fallen, it was Luce) for thousands of years. He remembers, she doesn't. That in itself is interesting. Luckily, the similarities end there, as I really did not like Fallen, if I could have given it negative stars I would have. However, I would give My Name is Memory 4. There were a few notable differences, and those made this one a much better read. <br /><br />Daniel and Lucy deal with complex emotions and are plagued with self doubt, and the story takes place over a lot of years. The corresponding back story, works with the current time frame so the reader can make sense of what has happened and what is happening. I've read all of Brashares other works of fiction and liked them all (expect the the 3 Willow, terrible). This one is not life changing, but definitely a solid summer read. This one may get made into a movie as well. I keep picturing a younger Brad Pitt for Daniel. I guess I'll just have to contend myself with watching A River Runs Through It.<br /><br />Just finished a reread of this one. On my second run through, I'd say that it's good but the ending really gets me. It makes it more of a 3 star than a 4 star book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11166064693863994551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_110694373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110694373" />
    <a title="Ronique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1457184-ronique"><img alt="Ronique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372459343p2/1457184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110694373?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronique" href="/user/show/1457184-ronique">Ronique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1457184-ronique?shelf=fic-series">fic-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer110694373&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110694373" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17693175048361409176">This could have been, (could have been) one of the best love stories I've read. This is includes Pride and Prejudice, which I hold in high regard as far as love/fiction is concerned. <br/><br/>I say could have been, not is, because of the conclusion to Daniel and Lucy's story. Thinking back, I should have expected a story that had two souls who were deeply connected yet never truly came together, to end this way. I was hoping for a resolution. A journey to the completion of their struggle to be together, </span>
  <span id="freeText17693175048361409176" style="display:none">This could have been, (could have been) one of the best love stories I've read. This is includes Pride and Prejudice, which I hold in high regard as far as love/fiction is concerned. <br /><br />I say could have been, not is, because of the conclusion to Daniel and Lucy's story. Thinking back, I should have expected a story that had two souls who were deeply connected yet never truly came together, to end this way. I was hoping for a resolution. A journey to the completion of their struggle to be together, finally, and at peace. <br /><br />No. No such ending. I was invested and really liked both of these lead characters, and bought the storyline. Learning about Daniel and how he coped with the memory of his many past lives, and Lucy coming to terms with her feelings and natural inclinations toward Daniel was interesting. The two finally getting together with all of the messiness between them was like watching the finish line get closer as you race toward it. And then. Then, you get to the last page, and realize it's over. It was like running the race of your life, deciding to say screw it, and walk home without finishing. I was disappointed in how this ended, needless to say.<br /><br />It's sad when a story can go from nearly amazing to just, 'meh'. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17693175048361409176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125308897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125308897" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1323522-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521352984p2/1323522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125308897?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/1323522-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125308897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer797847629073156923">One of the best books I've ever read. I was apprehensive at first from reading reviews of how slow the book started, but don't believe them! I was drawn into the story from page 1 and by a few chapters in I was so engrossed in the story I found myself reading at stop lights! <br/><br/>The story was original while still giving a wave to the likes of Time Traveler's Wife. For the most part, this story kept me guessing to the very end.<br/><br/>While reading I found holes and had lots of questions but Brashares' story</span>
  <span id="freeText797847629073156923" style="display:none">One of the best books I've ever read. I was apprehensive at first from reading reviews of how slow the book started, but don't believe them! I was drawn into the story from page 1 and by a few chapters in I was so engrossed in the story I found myself reading at stop lights! <br /><br />The story was original while still giving a wave to the likes of Time Traveler's Wife. For the most part, this story kept me guessing to the very end.<br /><br />While reading I found holes and had lots of questions but Brashares' story telling filled nearly all of those holes by the end in a nice pretty bow. And the ending...one of the best thus far. It left me on the edge, biting my nails for the next one while at the same time content with the characters' sories. <br /><br />This is certainly my favorite of Brashares' novels so far and have already recommended it to many friends. Her story telling and imagination make you feel like anything is possible without feeling crazy or too metaphorical, while still making you believe in God in heaven just from a different perspective. <br /><br />I actually finished this book with the thought of "Where's my time-travelling soul mate who loves me so much he would give his life?" Uh, huh, ya where is he??? I demand to know!</span>
  <a data-text-id="797847629073156923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1227786530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1227786530" />
    <a title="Eme Abarracoso" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28092603-eme-abarracoso"><img alt="Eme Abarracoso" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541921808p2/28092603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1227786530?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eme Abarracoso" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eme Abarracoso" href="/user/show/28092603-eme-abarracoso">Eme Abarracoso</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="paperback 9781594485183" href="/book/show/9750937-my-name-is-memory">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1227786530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17526797720533707820">I COULD STOP READING.I couldn't put it down! It was really that good!! This is the kind of book you want to burn throw out of the window after you finished reading. A no brainer, no a no-questions-asked hands-down 5-star rating! <br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Please believe him. Keep your heart open to him. He can make you happy. He has always loved you, and you once loved him with all your heart.” </blockquote>
  </i>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xZtA8LOLpK2sEDAL6Y4/T74weAzYtqn1qPa+Z9eY9bOFC4rG5VC0PbNJ1ABsnQt6kv4YDxXJ7mqvaI/7dtaEkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3d87d4igfwqTFexv0NysSQE9qhd2BCymxwVpSzgWeFadT/FB3ntvmoxMCGRVz5h8LfPKFLt7aznAm1jXmVgJdQ==')})
  }

Tornerà prossimamente in tutte le librerie.\n\nQuesta è una storia d\'amore ambientata nello schemat<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7525237413340993221\" style=\"display:none\">IMPORTANTE: i diritti di Come Petali di Ciliegio sono stati acquisiti da Newton Compton Editori, pertanto il libro non è più disponibile per l\'acquisto. Tornerà prossimamente in tutte le librerie.\n\nQuesta è una storia d\'amore ambientata nello schematico caos della poliedrica città di Tokyo. Una storia scandita dal lento cadere dei petali di ciliegio e dalla sensualità del kinbaku, o shibari, l\'arte di legare i corpi per esaltarne la bellezza. Una storia dove per trovare il vero amore è necessario squarciare la tela della vita quotidiana e guardare oltre. La storia di due anime legate dall\'indissolubile filo rosso del destino. A volte il confine tra giusto e sbagliato diventa così sottile. A volte è il destino che sceglie per te, che decide chi devi amare. E non puoi farci niente, non puoi resistere.   Quando Isabel è partita per studiare a Tokyo, si è portata dietro una valigia piena di determinazione e di fogli bianchi da riempire con i suoi disegni. Nella sua nuova vita da studentessa, non avrebbe mai immaginato di trovare l’amore. Ty è dolce, premuroso e passionale, il compagno ideale per affrontare un luogo così diverso da casa. Sarebbe una follia rischiare di perderlo. Sarebbe come squarciare la tela di un quadro perfetto. E se ci fosse qualcosa di tremendamente ammaliante, dietro a quella tela? Ryuu, il suo migliore amico, porta con sé il buio e la calma di un lago ghiacciato. Tratti misti e tutto il fascino dell\'Oriente, nei suoi occhi neri c\'è un abisso impenetrabile. Lui possiede qualcosa che Isabel desidera ardentemente: padroneggia un\'arte antica che la ossessiona, che cerca di riprodurre nei suoi disegni e che risveglia il lato più intenso della sua ispirazione.  Romanzo autoconclusivo.  Questo romanzo è la riedizione migliorata ed estesa de &quot;Il Filo Rosso del Destino&quot;, ritirato dallo store. In ancient times, people thought that the Sun, Moon, and star<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11659403062947300532\" style=\"display:none\">This fascinating narrative recounts the history of astronomy and, with more than 100 full-color illustrations, it shows readers how to find the planets and constellations in the night sky. In ancient times, people thought that the Sun, Moon, and stars were gods. They recorded their movements and imagined that the stars made pictures in the sky. The Greeks and the Romans related these &quot;pictures&quot; of animals and men—or constellations—to their legends. They also identified planets and named them for their gods—Venus, Mars, Saturn, and Jupiter. Their observations marked the first step in the development of astronomy, which today is a sophisticated science. Modern astronomers have followed the tradition of naming heavenly bodies after ancient gods. For instance, the solar system\'s outer planets weren\'t identified until after the telescope\'s invention, but with their discoveries they were named after Uranus, a Greek god of the sky . . . Neptune, the Roman god of the sea . . . and Pluto, the Roman god of the underworld. The author recounts the legends connected with many constellations, including Aquarius, Aries, Cancer, Orion, and others. This beautifully illustrated book helps readers navigate their way around the night sky as they learn the significance of heavenly bodies\' names. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5917040730965447697">Ann Brashares grew up in Chevy Chase, Maryland, with three brothers and attended a Quaker school in the D.C. area called Sidwell Friends. She studied Philosophy at Barnard College, part of Columbia University in New York City. Expecting to continue studying philosophy in graduate school, Ann took a year off after college to work as an editor, hoping to save money for school. Loving her job, she ne</span>
  <span id="freeText5917040730965447697" style="display:none">Ann Brashares grew up in Chevy Chase, Maryland, with three brothers and attended a Quaker school in the D.C. area called Sidwell Friends. She studied Philosophy at Barnard College, part of Columbia University in New York City. Expecting to continue studying philosophy in graduate school, Ann took a year off after college to work as an editor, hoping to save money for school. Loving her job, she never went to graduate school, and instead, remained in New York City and worked as an editor for many years. Ann made the transition from editor to full-time writer with her first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Sisterhood%20of%20the%20Traveling%20Pants" title=" The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants</a>. Ann and her husband live with their three children in New York.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5917040730965447697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
